  318. I had a slight learning curve using this mascara. It is basically a three step process (four if you curl your lashes). First you curl your lashes (optional), then you apply your own waterproof mascara (I used Great Lash waterproof), then you carefully layer the fibers and the gel (both included), you can repeat the layers to build your lashes. I found that it is important to only apply a little of the fiber each layer, otherwise there is the potential for eye irritation. When I get it right, I my short, thin eyelashes are transformed into long, fluttery lashes. And they actually look quite natural. I tested the &#34;waterproof&#34; claims by splashing water on my face and the mascara didn't budge. But it was easily removed with a little coconut oil and warm water. If you are patient and careful, this can be a great alternative to false eyelashes. I personally found it easier to apply than false eyelashes and the look is more natural.<br /><br />I did receive a sample of this product to review. I have never used fiber mascara before so this was my first experience with this type of product.

  365. I've tried several brands of the fiber-type mascaras. This is the only one that really works for me - gives me very long, full looking lashes, doesn't flake off all over my face and most importantly, doesn't leave my eyes feeling like I've stuck tiny needles into them like some kind of medieval torture routine. If you've not used this type of mascara system, it's a bit tricky at first & I think people get frustrated. You must follow the directions to the letter or you will be disappointed, worse yet you probably will feel like someone's stuck those tiny needles in your eyeballs. Per the instructions, do one eye at a time. This is essential because you apply the gel then quickly apply the fibers while the gel is still wet, wait about 20 seconds for the fibers to set then apply the gel again to seal in the fibers. The sequence is gel-fibers-gel. You can repeat these steps as often as you wish to get the desired effect. I find 2 total coats of the system gives me the look I want. One hint from my own experience - I find it helps to apply one coat of your regular mascara first before you begin the gel/fiber application then seal everything with a final coat of regular mascara. It helps keep the fibers locked in. My routine is regular mascara - gel - fibers - gel - fibers - gel - regular mascara. Hope that helps you too. This removes easily with soapy facial cleanser and water provided you're not using a waterproof mascara to seal the whole deal down. I've now purchased this twice, and have also found their customer service to be great.
